Tool calls:  [ToolUseBlock(id='toolu_01Rxfr4WmArd4VfVVaDk38Km', input={'coworker_name': 'Emily', 'message': 'Here\'s a beginner-friendly introduction to quantum computing:\n\n1. Quantum Bits (Qubits) and Superposition\n\nClassical Bit vs Qubit:\n- Classical bit: 0 OR 1\n- Qubit: Can be 0 AND 1 simultaneously (superposition)\n\nAnalogy: Think of a coin\n- Classical bit: Either heads or tails\n- Qubit: A spinning coin - simultaneously heads and tails until observed\n\nMathematical Representation:\n|ψ⟩ = α|0⟩ + β|1⟩\nwhere α² + β² = 1\n\n2. Quantum Gates and Circuits\n\nBasic Gates:\na) X Gate (NOT):\n- Flips the state of a qubit\n- Like a classical NOT gate\n- Represented by matrix: [[0,1],[1,0]]\n\nb) H Gate (Hadamard):\n- Creates superposition\n- Transforms |0⟩ to (|0⟩ + |1⟩)/√2\n- Transforms |1⟩ to (|0⟩ - |1⟩)/√2\n\nExample Circuit:\n```\n|0⟩ --[H]--[X]--\n```\n\n3. Quantum Entanglement and Teleportation\n\nEntanglement:\n- Two qubits linked regardless of distance\n- Measuring one instantly affects the other\n- Einstein called it "spooky action at a distance"\n\nAnalogy: Twin dice that always sum to 7\n- If one shows 6, the other must be 1\n- If one shows 2, the other must be 5\n\n4. Quantum Algorithms\n\nShor\'s Algorithm:\n- Purpose: Factor large numbers\n- Classical computers: Exponential time\n- Quantum computers: Polynomial time\n- Impact: Could break RSA encryption\n\nGrover\'s Algorithm:\n- Purpose: Search unstructured databases\n- Classical: O(N) time\n- Quantum: O(√N) time\n- Example: Finding a phone number in an unsorted directory\n\n5. Healthcare Applications\n\nDrug Discovery:\n- Simulate molecular interactions\n- Predict protein folding\n- Design new medications\n\nExample:\nClassical approach: Test millions of combinations\nQuantum approach: Simulate all combinations simultaneously\n\n6. Current Limitations\n\nHardware Challenges:\n- Decoherence (loss of quantum state)\n- Error rates\n- Limited qubit count\n- Need for extreme cooling\n\nPractical Example:\nToday\'s quantum computers:\n- ~100 noisy qubits\n- Need millions for practical applications\n- Error correction requires many physical qubits\n\nFuture Outlook:\n- Error correction improvements\n- Room temperature quantum computers\n- Hybrid classical-quantum systems\n\nWould you like me to elaborate on any of these topics or provide more examples?'}, name='help_coworker', type='tool_use')]
